                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insights into electrochemical process of hollow octahedral cobalt selenide on reduced graphene oxide for high-rate sodium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Zheng; Zhou, Shiyuan; Dai, Peng; Zeng, Ye; Huang, Ling; Liao, Hong-Gang; Sun, Shi-Gang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs), as an alternative and promising energy storage system, have attracted considerable attention due to the abundant reserves and low cost of sodium.  However, it remains a great challenge to achieve high capacity and rate capability required for practical applications.  Herein, hollow octahedral Co3Se4 particles encapsulated in reduced graphene oxide (Co3Se4@rGO) were designed and synthesized and exhibited excellent electrochem. performances as anodes of SIBs, esp. rate capability.  Sodiation/desodiation processes and involved mechanisms were investigated by using in situ TEM and in situ XRD.  During sodiation, a cryst. Na2Se layer with numerous amorphous fine Co nanoparticles dispersed on it was obsd. to appear on the surface of the original Co3Se4@rGO particles, and the movable Co-Na2Se composites further migrated to the rGO network with high electron/ion dual cond., resulting in ultrafast sodium storage kinetics and remarkable rate performance of the Co3Se4@rGO anode evidenced by delivering a discharge capacity of 229.3 mAh g-1 at a large c.d. of 50 A g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The pursuit of more efficient carbon-based anodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) prepd. from facile and economical methods is a very important endeavor.  Based on the crystallinity difference within carbon materials, herein, a low-temp. selective burning method is developed for prepg. oxygen and nitrogen codoped holey graphene aerogel as additive-free anode for SIBs.  By selective burning of a mixt. of graphene and low-crystallinity carbon at 450°C in air, an elastic porous graphene monolith with abundant holes on graphene sheets and optimized crystallinity is obtained.  These structural characteristics lead to an additive-free electrode with fast charge (ions and electrons) transfer and more abundant Na+ storage active sites.  Moreover, the heteroatom oxygen/nitrogen doping favors large interlayer distance for rapid Na+ insertion/extn. and provides more active sites for high capacitive contribution.  The optimized sample exhibits superior sodium-ion storage capability, i.e., high specific capacity (446 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), ultrahigh rate capability (189 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1), and long cycle life (81.0% capacity retention after 2000 cycles at 5 A g-1). Herein, cobalt chalcogenides (Co3O4, CoS, and Co3Se4) supported by reduced graphene oxide are synthesized as the electrode materials, which feature high cond., rapid kinetic conversion, and catalytic effect. Gradient structure is conducive to fast migration of electrons and ions with the association of ether electrolyte.  For half-cell, CoSe2@CNTs-MXene exhibits high initial coulomb efficiency (81.7%) and excellent cycling performance (400 mAh g(-1) cycling for 200 times in 2 A g(-1)).                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Molecular Coupling and Self-Assembly Strategy toward WSe2/Carbon Micro-Nano Hierarchical Structure for Elevated Sodium-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Ge; Ou, Xuewu; Yang, Jinghai; Tang, Yongbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small Methods</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium (Na) ion-based dual-ion batteries (Na-DIBs) have attracted great attention, owing to their benefits of low cost, high working voltage, and environmental friendliness.  However, the limited capacity and low tap d. of currently reported anode materials restrict the further improvement of Na-DIBs.  Herein, a micro-nano structure with vertically aligned WSe2 nanoflakes anchored tightly on a micron-sized carbon sphere (WSe2/CS) is successfully constructed via combining the mol. coupling and self-assembly strategy.  Within this hierarchical structure, the WSe2 nanoflakes can shorten the diffusion path for Na+ ions and alleviate structural deformation during the charge/discharge process; meanwhile, the micron-sized carbon core provides conductive support and helps improve the total tap d. of the anode electrode.  As a result, this micron-sized WSe2/CS displays a high specific capacity of ≈252.8 mAh g-1 and good cycling performance with ≈92% capacity retention after 1200 cycles.  Moreover, by pairing this WSe2/CS anode with environmental friendly graphite as cathode, a proof-of-concept Na-DIB shows 85.6% capacity retention after 1000 cycles, which is among the best performances of previously reported Na-DIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref49" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2020.03.007"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.                         cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational Design of Yolk-Shell ZnCoSe@N-Doped Dual Carbon Architectures as Long-Life and High-Rate Anodes for Half/Full Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Jian; Luo, Shao-hua; Yan, Sheng-xue; Zhan, Yang; Wang, Qing; Zhang, Ya-hui; Liu, Xin; Chang, Long-jiao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

Whereas, TMSs still suffer from poor rate capability and inferior cycling stability induced by sluggish kinetics and severe vol. changes during de/sodiation processes.  Herein, a hierarchical composite consisting of a zinc-cobalt bimetallic selenide yolk and nitrogen-doped double carbon shell (denoted as ZnCoSe@NDC) is engineered and fabricated successfully.  The architecture of the as-fabricated material improves the Na-ion storage performance via increasing the electron transfer kinetics, accommodating vol. expansion, and mitigating the generation of byproducts.  As expected, the ZnCoSe@NDC electrode delivers superior sodium storage performance with long cycling stability (344.5 mAh g-1 at 5.0 A g-1 over 2000 long-term cycles) and high-rate performance (319.2 mAh g-1 at 10.0 A g-1).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Because of their considerable theor. capacity and intrinsic cond., transition metal selenides have been considered as advanced electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, fast capacity fade and inferior rate performance still impede their large-scale application.  Herein, a hierarchically nitrogen-doped carbon (NC) wrapped binary transition metal selenide (Ni0.6Fe0.4Se2@NC, termed NFS@NC) nanomaterial derived from polydopamine coated Prussian blue analogs (Ni3[Fe(CN)6]2, Ni-Fe-PBA) was synthesized through a low-energy selenization and carbonization process.  The excellent morphol., large surface area, intimate contact of nanoparticles with the carbon matrix and better combination of binary metal selenides can achieve outstanding sodium storage performance through their synergy.  Notably, nitrogen-contg. compd. are efficiently converted to nitrogen-doped carbon with functional Fe-N-C bonds, facilitating the faster transfer of Na+.  As a result, the as-obtained NFS@NC showed superior rate performance (449.3 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 and 289.5 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1) and stable long-term cyclability (372.4 mA h g-1 after 2000 cycles at 5 A g-1) as an anode material for SIBs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium-ion battery has shown great potential to replace the lithium-ion battery, esp. for large-scale energy-storage systems. As an anode material in sodium-ion batteries, the as-fabricated Sb/N-CNN exhibits superior rate property (314 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1) and cycling stability (401 mAh g-1 after 6,000 cycles at 1 A g-1), outperforming other Sb-based materials.                         cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bimetallic Sulfide Sb2S3@FeS2 Hollow Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Liang; Gao, Xuanwen; Zhang, Bao; Ou, Xing; Zhang, Jiafeng; Luo, Wen-Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing a heterojunction and introducing an interfacial interaction by designing ideal structures have the inherent advantages of optimizing electronic structures and macroscopic mech. properties.  An exquisite hierarchical heterogeneous structure of bimetal sulfide Sb2S3@FeS2 hollow nanorods embedded into a nitrogen-doped carbon matrix is fabricated by a concise two-step solvothermal method.  The FeS2 interlayer expands in situ grow on the interface of hollow Sb2S3 nanorods within the nitrogen-doped graphene matrix, forming a delicate heterostructure.  Such a well-designed architecture affords rapid Na+ diffusion and improves charge transfer at the heterointerfaces.  Meanwhile, the strongly synergistic coupling interaction among the interior Sb2S3, interlayer FeS2, and external nitrogen-doped carbon matrix creates a stable nanostructure, which extremely accelerates the electronic/ion transport and effectively alleviates the vol. expansion upon long cyclic performance.  As a result, the composite, as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries, exhibits a superior rate capability of 537.9 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1 and excellent cyclic stability with 85.7% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  Based on the DFT calcn., the existing constructing heterojunction in this composite can not only optimize the electronic structure to enhance the cond. but also favor the Na2S adsorption energy to accelerate the reaction kinetics.  The outstanding electrochem. performance sheds light on the strategy by the rational design of hierarchical heterogeneous nanostructures for energy storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref60" class="refNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit60" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201902027"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G. B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, T. T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L. W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, J. X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effect of Crystal Structures on Electrochemical Performance of Hierarchically Porous CoSe<sub>2</sub> Spheres as Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemElectroChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">846</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">854</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/celc.201902027</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D7%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D846-854%26journal%3DChemElectroChem%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DG.%2BB.%2BXu%26author%3DT.%2BT.%2BCheng%26author%3DL.%2BW.%2BYang%26author%3DJ.%2BX.%2BCao%26title%3DEffect%2Bof%2BCrystal%2BStructures%2Bon%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BHierarchically%2BPorous%2BCoSe2%2BSpheres%2Bas%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fcelc.201902027&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c07118&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fcelc.201902027&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of Crystal Structures on Electrochemical Performance of Hierarchically Porous CoSe2 Spheres as Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xin; Xu, Guo B.; Cheng, Ting T.; Yang, Li W.; Cao, Jue X.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">846-854</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHEMRA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2196-0216</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal selenides with controllable crystal structures and hierarchically porous architectures have recently attracted great attention as the advanced electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  In present study, hierarchically porous orthogonal CoSe2 (o-CoSe2) and cubic CoSe2 (c-CoSe2) spheres are prepd. through a controllable selenization and subsequent annealing strategy.  Both types of CoSe2 spheres exhibit superior electrochem. properties resulting from hierarchical architecture, which can alleviate of the structural strain, the accelerated electron transmission and shorten the diffusion pathway of Na+.  As anode materials for SIBs, the o-CoSe2 electrode delivers a higher rate capability of 244 mAh g-1 at 3000 mA g-1 and a better cyclability of 378 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 1000 mA g-1 compared to the c-CoSe2.  From detailed microstructure characterization and kinetics behavior anal., it is revealed that the o-CoSe2 spheres exhibits larger sp. surface, optimized porous nature, higher pseudocapacitive contribution, and more powerful Na+-ions mobility.  Our studies can pave the way for rational design and development of selenides electrode materials in rechargeable batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref61" class="refNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit61" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2018.09.142"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhan, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Circuit board-like CoS/MXene composite with superior performance for sodium storage</span>. <i>Chem. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>357</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">220</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">225</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2018.09.142</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D357%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D220-225%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DR.%2BZhan%26author%3DQ.%2BXu%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DM.%2BTao%26author%3DY.%2BLuo%26author%3DS.%2BBao%26author%3DC.%2BLi%26author%3DM.%2BXu%26title%3DCircuit%2Bboard-like%2BCoS%252FMXene%2Bcomposite%2Bwith%2Bsuperior%2Bperformance%2Bfor%2Bsodium%2Bstorage%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2018.09.142&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c07118&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2018.09.142&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit61R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">61</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Circuit board-like CoS/MXene composite with superior performance for sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Youquan; Zhan, Renming; Xu, Qiuju; Liu, Heng; Tao, Mengli; Luo, Yushan; Bao, Shujuan; Li, Changming; Xu, Maowen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">357</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. performance of Ti3C2 MXene sheet is restricted by the modest specific capacity and self-restacking.  To conquer the defects, we designed cobalt sulfide and Ti3C2 MXene flake composite (CoS/MXene) with heterolayered architecture, in which ultrafine CoS nanoparticles (∼6 nm) were anchored on MXene flakes.  In this structure, the role of MXene is similar to printed circuit board, which providing conductive network.  As anode for sodium ion batteries, CoS/MXene electrode delivers a high reversible capacity of 267 mA h g-1 after 1700 cycles at 2 A g-1 with an extreme low capacity decay rate of only ∼0.0072% per cycle, and an outstanding rate performance with 272 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref62"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref62" class="refNumLink">62</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit62" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202003391"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jo, M. S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, J. S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jeong, S. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J. K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y. M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cho, J. S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Golden Bristlegrass-Like Hierarchical Graphene Nanofibers Entangled with N-Doped CNTs Containing CoSe<sub>2</sub> Nanocrystals at Each Node as Anodes for High-Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2003391</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smll.202003391</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D16%26publication_year%3D2020%26journal%3DSmall%26author%3DM.%2BS.%2BJo%26author%3DJ.%2BS.%2BLee%26author%3DS.%2BY.%2BJeong%26author%3DJ.%2BK.%2BKim%26author%3DY.%2BC.%2BKang%26author%3DD.%2BW.%2BKang%26author%3DS.%2BM.%2BJeong%26author%3DJ.%2BS.%2BCho%26title%3DGolden%2BBristlegrass-Like%2BHierarchical%2BGraphene%2BNanofibers%2BEntangled%2Bwith%2BN-Doped%2BCNTs%2BContaining%2BCoSe2%2BNanocrystals%2Bat%2BEach%2BNode%2Bas%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BHigh-Rate%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fsmll.202003391&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c07118&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fsmll.202003391&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit62R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">62</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Golden Bristlegrass-Like Hierarchical Graphene Nanofibers Entangled with N-Doped CNTs Containing CoSe2 Nanocrystals at Each Node as Anodes for High-Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jo, Min Su; Lee, Jae Seob; Jeong, Sun Young; Kim, Jae Kwang; Kang, Yun Chan; Kang, Dong Won; Jeong, Sang Mun; Cho, Jung Sang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">38</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2003391</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Golden bristlegrass-like unique nanostructures comprising reduced graphene oxide (rGO) matrixed nanofibers entangled with bamboo-like N-doped carbon nanotubes (CNTs) contg. CoSe2 nanocrystals at each node (denoted as N-CNT/rGO/CoSe2 NF) are designed as anodes for high-rate sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Bamboo-like N-doped CNTs (N-CNTs) are successfully generated on the rGO matrixed nanofiber surface, between rGO sheets and mesopores, and interconnected chem. with homogeneously distributed rGO sheets.  The defects in the N-CNTs formed by a simple etching process allow the complete phase conversion of Co into CoSe2 through the efficient penetration of H2Se gas inside the CNT walls.  The N-CNTs bridge the vertical defects for electron transfer in the rGO sheet layers and increase the distance between the rGO sheets during cycles.  The discharge capacity of N-CNT/rGO/CoSe2 NF after the 10 000th cycle at an extremely high c.d. of 10 A g-1 is 264 mA h g-1, and the capacity retention measured at the 100th cycle is 89%.  N-CNT/rGO/CoSe2 NF has final discharge capacities of 395, 363, 328, 304, 283, 263, 246, 223, 197, 171, and 151 mA h g-1 at current densities of 1, 2, 4, 6, 8, 10, 12, 14, 16, 18, and 20 A g-1, resp.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref63"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref63" class="refNumLink">63</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit63" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202207752"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pore Perforation of Graphene Coupled with In Situ Growth of Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub> for High-Performance Na-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>35</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2207752</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.202207752</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D35%26publication_year%3D2023%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DT.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DS.%2BCao%26author%3DR.%2BXiang%26author%3DL.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BYu%26title%3DPore%2BPerforation%2Bof%2BGraphene%2BCoupled%2Bwith%2BIn%2BSitu%2BGrowth%2Bof%2BCo3Se4%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BNa-Ion%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.202207752&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c07118&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.202207752&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit63R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">63</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pore Perforation of Graphene Coupled with In Situ Growth of Co3Se4 for High-Performance Na-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Tao; Yang, Yu; Cao, Shaowen; Xiang, Ronghua; Zhang, Liuyang; Yu, Jiaguo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">35</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2207752</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene-based nanomaterials have sprung up as promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries due to the intriguing properties of graphene itself and the synergic effect between graphene and active materials.  However, the 2D graphene sheet only allows the rapid diffusion of sodium ions along the parallel direction while that of the vertical direction is difficult, limiting the rate capability of graphene-based electrode materials.  To tackle this problem, pore-forming engineering has been employed to perforate graphene and concurrently achieve the in situ growth of Co3Se4 nanoparticles.  The generation of in-plane nanohole breaks through the phys. barriers of the graphene nanosheets, enabling the fast diffusion of electrolyte ions in the longitudinal direction.  In addn., this design limits the aggregation of Co3Se4 nanoparticles because of the high affinity of Co3Se4 on graphene.  Benefiting from the high cond. and fast ion transport bestowed by the ingenious architecture, the Co3Se4/holey graphene exhibits a remarkable rate performance of 519.5 mAh g-1 at 5.0 A g-1 and desirable cycle stability.  Conclusions drawn from this investigation are that the transport of sodium inside the graphene-based composites is crucial for rate performance enhancement and this method is effective in modifying graphene-based nanomaterials as potential anode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref64" class="refNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit64" data-doi="10.3866/PKU.WHXB202303046"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Holey Graphene for Sodium-Ion Battery Anode Material</span>. <i>Acta Phys.-Chim.                         rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Advances in Heterostructured Anode Materials with Multiple Anions for Advanced Alkali-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Gi Dae; Park, Jin-Sung; Kim, Jin Koo; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  As rechargeable battery technol. continues to advance, the development of advanced electrode materials is becoming increasingly crucial to meet the emerging demand for electrochem. energy storage devices with higher energy and power densities.  However, progress in anode materials has been sluggish and graphite is still widely applied in com. rechargeable batteries.  Alloying and conversion reaction-based anode materials, including Si, Sn, metal oxides, and metal chalcogenides, have been widely investigated as they exhibit much higher theor. capacities than carbonaceous materials.  However, they exhibit several intrinsic limitations, such as large vol. change, low elec. cond., and high voltage hysteresis.  Recently, the construction of heterostructures for anode materials has received increasing attention as it is an effective strategy to greatly enhance the capacity and rate performance by forming built-in elec. fields at the heterointerfaces, which can lower the activation energy for surface reactions.  This review introduces the recent progress in the development of heterostructured anode materials with an emphasis on metal compds. with multiple anions and various interpretations of the origin of their superior electrochem. properties in rechargeable alkali-ions (Li+, Na+, and K+) batteries.  The challenges and future outlook of advanced heterostructured anode materials research are discussed at the end of this review.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1016/j.xcrp.2020.100215"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Holey Graphene for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span>. <i>Cell Rep.                 10.1016/j.xcrp.2020.100215</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Holey Graphene for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Tao; Zhang, Liuyang; Cheng, Bei; Hu, Xianluo; Yu, Jiaguo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Cell Reports Physical Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Inc.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Graphene and its hybrids have been considered promising candidates for electrochem. energy storage because of their fascinating physicochem. properties.  However, they suffer from unsatisfactory areal or volumetric energy d. and relatively poor rate performance.  These drawbacks are due to limited accessible surface area and poor ion diffusion capacity arising from the agglomeration and restacking of graphene nanosheets during electrode assembly.  To solve the above issues, perforation on the graphene planes is adopted, which bestows the graphene-based nanomaterials with porous architectures.  In particular, in-plane holes are capable of accelerating ion transport across the graphene sheets and ultimately accessing the inner electrode surface.  Here, a comprehensive of holey graphene-based nanomaterials is presented, which summarizes recent progress from their rational design and controlled synthesis to their applications in electrochem. energy storage.  Finally, perspectives on the future directions of their large-scale synthesis and advanced assembly protocols as electrodes are proposed and discussed.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1016/j.jmst.2020.08.030"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, H.                         rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Freestanding nanosheets of 1T-2H hybrid MoS2 as electrodes for efficient sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Haiyang; Wang, Zhenzhu; Ni, Jiangfeng; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Science &amp; Technology (Shenyang, China)</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Editorial Board of Journal of Materials Science &amp; Technology</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) is a promising electrode material for sodium-ion batteries as it offers a large capacity through a distinct conversion reaction.  However, the electrochem. potential of MoS2 is often restrained by the poor cond. as the dominant 2 H phase is a semiconductor while the metallic1 T phase is thermodynamically unstable.  In this work, we report a hybrid design and material prepn. of freestanding nanosheets of MoS2 composed of both 1 T and 2 H phases based on mild hydrothermal reaction.  The introduction of the metallic 1 T-MoS2 phase into 2 H-MoS2 and their intimate hybridization enable a significant improvement in electronic cond., while the freestanding architecture avoids possible electrochem. aggregation.  When used as electrodes for sodium storage, such a hybrid MoS2 affords a high capacity of ∼500 mA h g-1 at 0.5 A g-1 after 300 cycles, and retains capacity of ∼200 mA h g-1 at a high current rate of 4 A g-1, thus demonstrating their potential in high-performance battery applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1038/srep07231"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alonso, J.                         rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Experimental visualization of the diffusion pathway of sodium ions in the Na3[Ti2P2O10F] anode for sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Zhaohui; Wang, Yuesheng; Sun, Chunwen; Alonso, J.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have attracted considerable interest as an alternative to lithium-ion batteries for elec. storage applications because of the low cost and natural abundance of sodium resources.  The materials with an open framework are highly desired for Na-ion insertion/extn.  Here we report on the first visualization of the sodium-ion diffusion path in Na3[Ti2P2O10F] through high-temp. neutron powder diffraction expts.  The evolution of the Na-ion displacements of Na3[Ti2P2O10F] was investigated with high-temp. neutron diffraction (HTND) from room temp. to 600°C; difference Fourier maps were utilized to est. the Na nuclear-d. distribution.  Temp.-driven Na displacements indicates that sodium-ion diffusion paths are established within the ab plane.  As an anode for sodium-ion batteries, Na3[Ti2P2O10F] exhibits a reversible capacity of ∼100 mAh g-1 with lower intercalation voltage.  It also shows good cycling stability and rate capability, making it promising applications in sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2022.141424"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A high-performance solid sodium battery enabled by a thin Na-Ti<sub>3</sub>C2T<sub><i>x</i></sub> composite anode</span>. <i>Electrochim. Large volumetric variations during the discharging/charging and intrinsically poor elec. cond., however, severely hinder its application.  Herein, a core-shell structured composite is constructed by hollow carbon spheres and SiO2 nanosheets decorated with nickel nanoparticles (Ni-SiO2/C HS).  Hollow carbon spheres, as mesoporous cores, not only significantly facilitate the electron transfer but also prominently enhance the mech. robustness of anode materials, which sep. improves the rate performance and the cyclic durability.  Besides, ultrathin SiO2 nanosheets, as hierarchical shells, provide abundant electrochem. active surface for capacity increment. Such a unique architecture of Ni-SiO2/C HS guarantees an enhanced discharge capacity (712 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1) and prolonged cyclic durability (352 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 after 500 cycles).         </div><div class="casAbstract">The pore structural designability of wood-derived hard carbons (WDHCs) lays an optimal foundation for acquiring a cost-efficient and green anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  Here, a WDHCs material was reported for high-capacity and cycling-stable sodium storage through a pore forming-opening strategy.  Assocd. with the natural holey texture of wood, the WDHCs displays a hierarchical pore structure by a precise chem. treatment and a high-temp. carbonization, creating the straight channels and plentiful closed nanopores. The employment of the MXene parent phase exhibits distinctive advantages, enabling defect engineering, nanoengineering, and fluorine-doped metal oxides.  As a result, the M-TiO2@rGO electrode shows a pseudocapacitance-dominated hybrid sodium storage mechanism.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium hybrid supercapacitors (Na-HSCs) are regarded as one promising electrochem. energy storage device, because of the low price of sodium, prolonged life cycle, and high-energy/power d.  Nonetheless, the imparity between the fast capacitive reactions at cathode and the sluggish Faradaic reactions at the anode leads to an imbalance in the electrochem. reaction kinetics, limiting the development of Na-HSCs.  Therefore, it is urgent to develop suitable anode materials for performance-enhanced Na-HSCs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">As typical 2D materials, VSe2 and MoSe2 both play a complementary role in Li/Na/K storage.  Therefore, we designed and optimized the VSe2/MoSe2 heterostructure to gain highly efficient Li/Na/K-ion batteries.  Most importantly, achieving fast Li/Na/K-ion diffusion kinetics in the interlayer of VSe2/MoSe2 is a key point.  First of all, first-principles calcns. were carried out to systematically investigate the packing structure, mech. properties, band structure, and Li/Na/K storage mechanism. These structures were all further verified to show thermal stability (300 K) by means of the AIMD method.  By analyzing the Li/Na/K diffusion behavior and the effect of vacancy defect on the structural stability and energy barrier for Li interlayer diffusion, it is found that the VSe2/MoSe2 heterostructure exhibits very low-energy barriers for Na/K interlayer diffusion (0.21 eV for Na and 0.11 eV for K). Based on the band energy theory, a route to enhance the rate ability for electrode is exploited on regulating interfaces of substrates/active heterojunction.  Herein, the highly stable Na+-storage performance of GeS2/3DG is delicately designed, where the hierarchical structure is enabled by uniformly overcoating GeS2 nanograins with graphene matrix.  Different from the widespread doping route of active materials for fast ion transfer, we focus on the effects of interface regulation on the high-rate Na- ion-storage performance of substrate/active materials.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus has received remarkable attention as a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (NIBs) due to its high theor. capacity.  However, its practical application has been impeded by its intrinsic low electronic cond. and large vol. variations during sodiation/desodiation process.  Here, we design a composite to confine nanosized red phosphorus into the hierarchically porous carbon (HPC) walls by a vaporization-condensation strategy. Herein, Co3Se4 quantum dots (QD) encapsulated by N-doped carbon (CSC) are reported as an anode material for KIBs, in which a morphol. change process occurs. With the comparison of traditional MoSe2/C composite, the sandwich structured MoSe2 with double carbon coating can bring multi-ion/electron transportation channels, favoring the Na+ storage and charge transfer kinetics.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sn-based chalcogenides are considered as one of the most promising anode materials for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) because of their high capacities through both conversion and alloying reactions.  However, the realization of full capacities of Sn-based chalcogenides is mainly hindered by the large vol. variation and inferior reversibility of conversion reaction during cycling.  In present work, a new ternary SnSMo-graphene nanosheets (SnS-Mo-GNs) composite is fabricated by a simple and scalable plasma milling method, in which SnS nanoparticles are tightly bonded with Mo and GNs. This work reveals that high rate Li-ion batteries can be achieved through constructing the hybrids of Co3O4 nanocrystals on in situ etched holey graphene, while rendering fundamental for enhancement of mass transport rate by highly shortened ions diffusion distance in a nanostructured electrode to accomplish superior rate capability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref50" class="rightTabRefNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit50" data-doi="10.1016/j.est.2022.104522"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nickel-cobalt Selenide@N-doped Carbon towards High-performance Anode Materials for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Whereas, TMSs still suffer from poor rate capability and inferior cycling stability induced by sluggish kinetics and severe vol. changes during de/sodiation processes.  Herein, a hierarchical composite consisting of a zinc-cobalt bimetallic selenide yolk and nitrogen-doped double carbon shell (denoted as ZnCoSe@NDC) is engineered and fabricated successfully.  The architecture of the as-fabricated material improves the Na-ion storage performance via increasing the electron transfer kinetics, accommodating vol. expansion, and mitigating the generation of byproducts.  As expected, the ZnCoSe@NDC electrode delivers superior sodium storage performance with long cycling stability (344.5 mAh g-1 at 5.0 A g-1 over 2000 long-term cycles) and high-rate performance (319.2 mAh g-1 at 10.0 A g-1).  Meanwhile, the NVP@C//ZnCoSe@NDC full SIB cells are constructed successfully, retaining 96.3% of its initial capacity at 0.5A g-1 after 200 loops. T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y. C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">N-Doped Carbon Nanonecklaces with Encapsulated Sb as a Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span>. <i>Matter</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">720</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">733</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.matt.2019.03.010</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N-Doped Carbon Nanonecklaces with Encapsulated Sb as a Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jing, Wen Tao; Zhang, Ying; Gu, Yan; Zhu, Yong Fu; Yang, Chun Cheng; Jiang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Matter</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">720-733</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MATTCG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2590-2385</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Inc.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium-ion battery has shown great potential to replace the lithium-ion battery, esp. for large-scale energy-storage systems.  In this work, a hybrid material of ultra-small Sb nanoparticles encapsulated in unique N-doped carbon nanonecklace (Sb/N-CNN) has been synthesized for the first time via electrospinning and in situ substitution.  As an anode material in sodium-ion batteries, the as-fabricated Sb/N-CNN exhibits superior rate property (314 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1) and cycling stability (401 mAh g-1 after 6,000 cycles at 1 A g-1), outperforming other Sb-based materials.  Such excellent performances originate from the ingenious necklace-like structure of Sb/N-CNN, which supplies efficient electrolyte diffusion paths and more active sites for Na+ insertion/extn., disperses the stress caused by the large vol. change of Sb nanoparticles during the cycling process, and also reduces the electrode resistance.  This study provides a facile strategy for construction of a well-designed structure for advanced energy-storage technologies.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref59" class="rightTabRefNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit59" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c00020"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bimetallic Sulfide Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@FeS<sub>2</sub> Hollow Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3610</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3620</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.0c00020</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bimetallic Sulfide Sb2S3@FeS2 Hollow Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Liang; Gao, Xuanwen; Zhang, Bao; Ou, Xing; Zhang, Jiafeng; Luo, Wen-Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3610-3620</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing a heterojunction and introducing an interfacial interaction by designing ideal structures have the inherent advantages of optimizing electronic structures and macroscopic mech. properties.  An exquisite hierarchical heterogeneous structure of bimetal sulfide Sb2S3@FeS2 hollow nanorods embedded into a nitrogen-doped carbon matrix is fabricated by a concise two-step solvothermal method.  The FeS2 interlayer expands in situ grow on the interface of hollow Sb2S3 nanorods within the nitrogen-doped graphene matrix, forming a delicate heterostructure.  Such a well-designed architecture affords rapid Na+ diffusion and improves charge transfer at the heterointerfaces.  Meanwhile, the strongly synergistic coupling interaction among the interior Sb2S3, interlayer FeS2, and external nitrogen-doped carbon matrix creates a stable nanostructure, which extremely accelerates the electronic/ion transport and effectively alleviates the vol. expansion upon long cyclic performance.  As a result, the composite, as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries, exhibits a superior rate capability of 537.9 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1 and excellent cyclic stability with 85.7% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  Based on the DFT calcn., the existing constructing heterojunction in this composite can not only optimize the electronic structure to enhance the cond. but also favor the Na2S adsorption energy to accelerate the reaction kinetics.  The outstanding electrochem. performance sheds light on the strategy by the rational design of hierarchical heterogeneous nanostructures for energy storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref60" class="rightTabRefNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit60" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201902027"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G. B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, T. T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L. W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, J. X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effect of Crystal Structures on Electrochemical Performance of Hierarchically Porous CoSe<sub>2</sub> Spheres as Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemElectroChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">846</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">854</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/celc.201902027</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of Crystal Structures on Electrochemical Performance of Hierarchically Porous CoSe2 Spheres as Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xin; Xu, Guo B.; Cheng, Ting T.; Yang, Li W.; Cao, Jue X.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">846-854</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHEMRA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2196-0216</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal selenides with controllable crystal structures and hierarchically porous architectures have recently attracted great attention as the advanced electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  In present study, hierarchically porous orthogonal CoSe2 (o-CoSe2) and cubic CoSe2 (c-CoSe2) spheres are prepd. through a controllable selenization and subsequent annealing strategy.  Both types of CoSe2 spheres exhibit superior electrochem. properties resulting from hierarchical architecture, which can alleviate of the structural strain, the accelerated electron transmission and shorten the diffusion pathway of Na+.  As anode materials for SIBs, the o-CoSe2 electrode delivers a higher rate capability of 244 mAh g-1 at 3000 mA g-1 and a better cyclability of 378 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 1000 mA g-1 compared to the c-CoSe2.  From detailed microstructure characterization and kinetics behavior anal., it is revealed that the o-CoSe2 spheres exhibits larger sp. surface, optimized porous nature, higher pseudocapacitive contribution, and more powerful Na+-ions mobility.  Our studies can pave the way for rational design and development of selenides electrode materials in rechargeable batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref61" class="rightTabRefNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit61" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2018.09.142"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhan, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Circuit board-like CoS/MXene composite with superior performance for sodium storage</span>. <i>Chem. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>357</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">220</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">225</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2018.09.142</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit61R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">61</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Circuit board-like CoS/MXene composite with superior performance for sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Youquan; Zhan, Renming; Xu, Qiuju; Liu, Heng; Tao, Mengli; Luo, Yushan; Bao, Shujuan; Li, Changming; Xu, Maowen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">357</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">220-225</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. performance of Ti3C2 MXene sheet is restricted by the modest specific capacity and self-restacking.  To conquer the defects, we designed cobalt sulfide and Ti3C2 MXene flake composite (CoS/MXene) with heterolayered architecture, in which ultrafine CoS nanoparticles (∼6 nm) were anchored on MXene flakes.  In this structure, the role of MXene is similar to printed circuit board, which providing conductive network.  As anode for sodium ion batteries, CoS/MXene electrode delivers a high reversible capacity of 267 mA h g-1 after 1700 cycles at 2 A g-1 with an extreme low capacity decay rate of only ∼0.0072% per cycle, and an outstanding rate performance with 272 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref62"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref62" class="rightTabRefNumLink">62</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit62" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202003391"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jo, M. S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, J. S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jeong, S. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J. K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y. C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, D. W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jeong, S. M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cho, J. S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Golden Bristlegrass-Like Hierarchical Graphene Nanofibers Entangled with N-Doped CNTs Containing CoSe<sub>2</sub> Nanocrystals at Each Node as Anodes for High-Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2003391</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smll.202003391</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit62R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">62</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Golden Bristlegrass-Like Hierarchical Graphene Nanofibers Entangled with N-Doped CNTs Containing CoSe2 Nanocrystals at Each Node as Anodes for High-Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jo, Min Su; Lee, Jae Seob; Jeong, Sun Young; Kim, Jae Kwang; Kang, Yun Chan; Kang, Dong Won; Jeong, Sang Mun; Cho, Jung Sang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">38</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2003391</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Golden bristlegrass-like unique nanostructures comprising reduced graphene oxide (rGO) matrixed nanofibers entangled with bamboo-like N-doped carbon nanotubes (CNTs) contg. CoSe2 nanocrystals at each node (denoted as N-CNT/rGO/CoSe2 NF) are designed as anodes for high-rate sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Bamboo-like N-doped CNTs (N-CNTs) are successfully generated on the rGO matrixed nanofiber surface, between rGO sheets and mesopores, and interconnected chem. with homogeneously distributed rGO sheets.  The defects in the N-CNTs formed by a simple etching process allow the complete phase conversion of Co into CoSe2 through the efficient penetration of H2Se gas inside the CNT walls.  The N-CNTs bridge the vertical defects for electron transfer in the rGO sheet layers and increase the distance between the rGO sheets during cycles.  The discharge capacity of N-CNT/rGO/CoSe2 NF after the 10 000th cycle at an extremely high c.d. of 10 A g-1 is 264 mA h g-1, and the capacity retention measured at the 100th cycle is 89%.  N-CNT/rGO/CoSe2 NF has final discharge capacities of 395, 363, 328, 304, 283, 263, 246, 223, 197, 171, and 151 mA h g-1 at current densities of 1, 2, 4, 6, 8, 10, 12, 14, 16, 18, and 20 A g-1, resp.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref63"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref63" class="rightTabRefNumLink">63</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit63" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202207752"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pore Perforation of Graphene Coupled with In Situ Growth of Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub> for High-Performance Na-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>35</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2207752</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.202207752</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit63R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">63</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pore Perforation of Graphene Coupled with In Situ Growth of Co3Se4 for High-Performance Na-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Tao; Yang, Yu; Cao, Shaowen; Xiang, Ronghua; Zhang, Liuyang; Yu, Jiaguo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">35</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2207752</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene-based nanomaterials have sprung up as promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries due to the intriguing properties of graphene itself and the synergic effect between graphene and active materials.  However, the 2D graphene sheet only allows the rapid diffusion of sodium ions along the parallel direction while that of the vertical direction is difficult, limiting the rate capability of graphene-based electrode materials.  To tackle this problem, pore-forming engineering has been employed to perforate graphene and concurrently achieve the in situ growth of Co3Se4 nanoparticles.  The generation of in-plane nanohole breaks through the phys. barriers of the graphene nanosheets, enabling the fast diffusion of electrolyte ions in the longitudinal direction.  In addn., this design limits the aggregation of Co3Se4 nanoparticles because of the high affinity of Co3Se4 on graphene.  Benefiting from the high cond. and fast ion transport bestowed by the ingenious architecture, the Co3Se4/holey graphene exhibits a remarkable rate performance of 519.5 mAh g-1 at 5.0 A g-1 and desirable cycle stability.  Conclusions drawn from this investigation are that the transport of sodium inside the graphene-based composites is crucial for rate performance enhancement and this method is effective in modifying graphene-based nanomaterials as potential anode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref64" class="rightTabRefNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit64" data-doi="10.3866/PKU.WHXB202303046"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Holey Graphene for Sodium-Ion Battery Anode Material</span>. <i>Acta Phys.-Chim. Sin.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>39</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2303046</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.3866/PKU.WHXB202303046</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i21">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.3c07118?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.3c07118</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Material characterization; electrochemical measurements; and additional SEM, XRD, TG, XPS, CV, and long-cycle performance (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c07118/suppl_file/am3c07118_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c07118/suppl_file/am3c07118_si_001.pdf">am3c07118_si_001.pdf (1.27 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

        <script nonce="931883114e6354b8-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="931883114e6354b8-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>

<script nonce="931883114e6354b8-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());

        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");

          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

        <script nonce="931883114e6354b8-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
